1990 - Jolly Salah: boss in pipe-lining it works as follows : 
1) client sends TCP req to the server 
2) server replies to the TCP req 

( SO , 1 & 2 makes One RTT ) 

and then :
3) client sends HTTP req 
4) server replies with the HTML file 

(again 3 & 4 makes another RTT )

Finally :
5) all remaining objects are sent using only 1 HTTP req 
6)server replies to all of them also in 1 HTTP response 

(and this makes the 3rd RTT ) 

Fahem 7aga ? :D

2192 - Mohamed El Menisy: verifyH1 (Impl a(Impl b c)) = if(a==c) then True else False
verifyH2 (Impl (Impl a (Impl b c)) (Impl (Impl d e) (Impl f g))) = if( a==d && a==f && b==e && c==g) then True else False
verifyH3 ((Impl (Impl (Impl a Bot) Bot) b)) =  if(a==b) then True else False

verifyAxiom stmt = ((verifyH1 stmt) || (verifyH3 stmt) || (verifyH2 stmt))

2478 - Mohamed El Menisy: btw fe 7eta aretha 3ala wiki it may help u understand aktar the difference between RGB n CMYK

2479 - Mohamed El Menisy: here

2480 - Mohamed El Menisy: RGB uses additive color mixing, because it describes what kind of light needs to be emitted to produce a given color. Light is added together to create form from out of the darkness. RGB stores individual values for red, green and blue. RGBA is RGB with an additional channel, alpha, to indicate transparency.
Common color spaces based on the RGB model include sRGB, Adobe RGB and ProPhoto RGB.

CMYK uses subtractive color mixing used in the printing process, because it describes what kind of inks need to be applied so the light reflected from the substrate and through the inks produces a given color. One starts with a white substrate (canvas, page, etc.), and uses ink to subtract color from white to create an image. CMYK stores ink values for cyan, magenta, yellow and black. There are many CMYK color spaces for different sets of inks, substrates, and press characteristics (which change the dot gain or transfer function for each ink and thus change the appearance).

2867 - Mohamed El Menisy: u run the server

2868 - Mohamed El Menisy: then u run a client

2869 - Mohamed El Menisy: let the client chat to the server

2870 - Mohamed El Menisy: n then let the server reply back

2871 - Mohamed El Menisy: now create a new client

2873 - Mohamed El Menisy: n reply back "now the server should reply back to the second client"

2874 - Mohamed El Menisy: n now ba2a

2875 - Mohamed El Menisy: whoever talks to the server "one of the 2 clients" the server should reply to him

2876 - Mohamed El Menisy: n this will apply for any number of clients
